Palestine: Situation Slightly Calmer 49

Arab Armed Bands Indiscriminately Harassing; British Warships Arrive at Jaffa Port to Suppress Unrest

(London) Lieutenant General Wauchope, the British High Commissioner for Palestine, reported to the British government today that the situation throughout Palestine is significantly calmer than before. The British warship HMS Barham, flying the flag of British Admiral Pound, has now arrived at Jaffa. It is reported that the area is generally peaceful, except for occasional burning of Jewish crops and occasional shootings. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Jerusalem: Armed Arab bands are now even more audacious, especially in northern Palestine. Their actions are gradually resembling an uprising against the government. They often lie in ambush to attack individuals and shoot at mechanized convoys with armed guards. Many Jewish farmers' crops have been burned, and telephone lines are frequently cut, causing this city to be unable to communicate with Haifa and Cairo yesterday. It is now believed that Arab leaders are preparing to call off the strike and curb the riots, as they are gradually realizing that they cannot control the zealous youths. However, High Commissioner Wauchope has refused to make any concessions on the main points of his policy, resolving to begin negotiations only after the unrest is quelled. It is difficult to find a mutually agreeable solution to immediately resolve the current unrest and calm the atmosphere so that both sides can negotiate. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

(Cairo) Due to the increasingly serious situation in Palestine, the British authorities today resolved to send British troops to the area again. However, there is no question of sending a large number of reinforcements at present; approximately no more than one company will be sent. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

(London) Dominion Secretary Malcolm MacDonald replied to a question in the House of Commons today that there are still sporadic acts of violence in Palestine, so the region is not yet peaceful. According to newspaper reports, the most serious riots occurred in Gaza yesterday, but he is certain that order has been restored there. In addition to implementing various riot prevention plans, the High Commissioner is now also restricting the activities of agitators and strike leaders. At the beginning of this year, the authorities permitted an increase in British and Palestinian police. The High Commissioner has recently recruited former police officers to form a supplementary police force. Since the outbreak of the unrest, the troops stationed there have been greatly increased. The proposal to select a Royal Commission to thoroughly investigate the matter after order is restored throughout the region will not be opposed by the public. However, its terms of reference and personnel have not yet been announced. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Swedish Parliament Debates Foreign Policy 50

Safeguarding the International Rule of Law System Held as a Fundamental Belief

Stockholm, Sweden: During today's session of the Lower House, Conservative Party member Bach questioned the current international situation. Foreign Minister Sandler replied, stating in brief: "Looking at the current international situation, we should deeply study the current system and mode of action of the League of Nations, as well as the possibility of expanding the scope of cooperation among countries to safeguard peace. We have gained experience from the Abyssinian question and are therefore hesitant and at a loss as to how to implement sanctions in the future and how they should be implemented. What we should deeply study at this moment is, of course, the question of whether the content of certain articles of the League of Nations Covenant and their implementation methods should be revised. In addition, we should also pay attention to how these articles interact with each other. The purpose of this is none other than to enhance the League of Nations' power to act in order to eliminate war. Fortunately, some major countries are sometimes willing to take on the task of eliminating war. In the future, we should strive to create conditions for the cooperation of major countries and make them more universal. As for the small countries, the following principles are tied to their fundamental beliefs. What are these principles? The League of Nations Covenant and the policies adopted are only for the purpose of safeguarding the public interest and safeguarding the international rule of law system, and this policy should be implemented uniformly for all issues. Although a neutral policy can also maintain security, its effectiveness is difficult to compare with other tools, such as a policy of solidarity and unity. Considering our own country, we should adopt a firm stance on international issues that have a direct interest to our country or when other countries make legitimate appeals to our country, so as to participate in cooperation for the international rule of law system. Otherwise, we should stay out of it. Based on this, although our country should cooperate closely with other countries, the attitude we adopt should be "the same as those countries, and we do not want to be unique." During today's discussion, one left-wing member argued that Sweden should withdraw from the League of Nations, but other members did not support his view. (Havas News Agency, 26th)

Belgian Cabinet Resigns

Brussels: The Belgian Cabinet met at 4:30 p.m. and all cabinet members signed their resignation letters. Prime Minister Janson presented them to King Leopold III at the palace at 9:00 p.m. Transport Minister Spaak declared that a new cabinet could be formed quickly. Political circles believe that the King will still entrust Prime Minister Janson to form a new cabinet, but whether the Prime Minister is willing to obey is still undecided. If Janson refuses to accept, the task of forming a cabinet will be given to the leader of the Socialist Party, the current Minister without Portfolio, Mr. Vandervelde. However, the Christian Social Party, the Liberal Party, and the Socialist Party (the three major parties that make up the current cabinet) all advocate that the future cabinet should still be formed by Janson. (Havas News Agency, 26th)

Xiang River Bursts; Zhongxiang Remote Dike Collapses 51

(Hankou) The Xiang River burst its banks, and 36 sections of the tenth section of the Zhongxiang Remote Dike collapsed on the evening of the 26th. On the 27th, it gradually stabilized. The Yangjia Hong was flooded, and the Hanyi Road was cut off. (Special dispatch, 27th)

(Hankou) The Xiang River rose abruptly by more than a丈 (unit of measurement, approx. 3.3 meters) on the 25th and 26th. The water level at Zhao Jiaqiao on the Xiang Dike rose to 45 meters, and the water barrier was in danger. After strenuous efforts to rescue it, it finally collapsed on the evening of the 26th. Currently, the Remote Dike is being rescued. The Xiangyang Flood Relief Association telegraphed on the evening of the 26th that a section of the Black Dragon Temple on the Laolong Dike was in danger. Due to the rising water and rapid flow, many cracks were found. Please quickly instruct the dike engineering bureau there to urgently repair it. (Special dispatch, 27th)

(Nanjing) Xi Dejiong, Director of the Jianghan Engineering Bureau, received a telegram from the Xiang Dike Engineering Office stating that the water level in Yunyang rose abruptly by approximately 7 meters on the 26th, and the water level in Xiangyang had reached above 13 meters, an abrupt rise of approximately 4 meters compared to the 25th, breaking the record for the same period in previous years. It is predicted that when the water reaches Zhongxiang, the water level must rise sharply, exceeding 45 meters. It was found that after the breach at the third and fourth sections last year was blocked this spring, a water barrier was built, with its top point reaching only 45 meters. It is bound to overflow and collapse. The Remote Dike project, which is under construction, is nearing completion and is extremely precarious. The workers are currently racing against time to rescue it, etc. After receiving the telegram, Xi immediately flew back to Hankou and then to the construction site to supervise the defense of the Remote Dike. The Committee also sent Wang Huzhen and Yan Honggui to fly to the construction site to survey the situation and jointly discuss remedial measures. At the same time, they telegraphed the Hubei Provincial Government and ordered the Yangtze River Commission to simultaneously dispatch specialists to quickly find a way to save the situation. (Special dispatch, 27th)

Yangtze River Conservancy Association Convenes Flood Prevention Conference 52

Representatives from Six Provinces and Cities Arrive and Resolve Important Cases

(Nanjing) The Yangtze River Conservancy Association convened a flood prevention conference at 2:00 p.m. on the 27th, gathering representatives from Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, and the City of Nanjing. The conference was convened because the Yangtze River below Hankou, in areas such as Jiujiang, Xunyang, Anqing, and Wuhu, has experienced high base water levels due to heavy rainfall this spring, and the recent rise in water level has been rapid, comparable to the water level during the same period in the 20th year of the Republic (1931). The dike restoration work in Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui provinces this year was delayed due to spring rains, and the arrival of the water this year was early. The conference aimed to coordinate flood prevention work. The attendees included Liu Yiyan, Director of the Anhui Construction Department, Wen Yi, Technical Officer, Yan Fangtian, Director of the Jiangxi Water Conservancy Bureau, Qiu Baozhong, Chief Engineer, Xi Dejiong, representative of Hubei, Lin Baoyuan, representative of Jiangsu, Song Xishang, representative of Nanjing, Zheng Zhaojing of the Economic Committee's Water Conservancy Department, and Xu Baoju, Chief of the Yangtze River Conservancy Association's General Affairs Department. Fu Rulin, the chairman, delivered the opening speech. The Economic Committee's representative then delivered a speech. The representatives reported in turn on the flood prevention process last year, the achievements of this year's dike restoration project, and the preparations for this year's flood prevention. After the reports, various proposals were discussed, and the following important cases were resolved: 1. Whether the general outline of the Yangtze River flood prevention measures should be revised. It was resolved to pass the revised version. 2. Song Xishang proposed that the Yangtze River Conservancy Commission should telegraph the daily water level along the river to the provincial and municipal governments during the flood season. It was resolved that the association should send a letter to the Central Broadcasting Station requesting it to report the water level on time and broadcast the rainfall reports simultaneously. 3. Anhui, Hunan, Jiangxi, and the City of Nanjing jointly proposed how to request subsidies and allocate flood prevention funds this year. It was resolved that the association should submit a request to the central government to prepare 200,000 yuan in flood prevention funds this year and issue them to the provincial and municipal governments for planning and management at the dangerous water level. 4. The Anhui Provincial Government proposed matters to be handled for flood prevention and requested that the amount of subsidies for flood prevention in other provinces be determined and allocated. It was resolved that items 1, 2, 3, and 4 of the proposal had been reported in detail, and item 5, the protection of dike workers, should be handled separately. The meeting concluded at 6:00 p.m. and a group photo was taken. (Central News Agency dispatch, 27th)

Wu Dingchang Talks About the Reasons for Establishing a Fish Market by the Ministry of Industries 60

Fish Merchants Can Buy and Sell Freely, Not Under Unified Control; Vegetable Oil Plant is Cooperation with Merchants

(Nanjing) Wu Dingchang, Minister of Industry, issued the following statement on the 27th: In recent days, foreign newspapers have been unclear about the truth regarding the undertakings handled by the Ministry, such as the Shanghai fish market and the vegetable oil plant, and have either called them unified control or mistaken them for monopolies. According to the facts, this is not true. The reason why the Ministry established the fish market is that the supply of fish food to the millions of citizens of Shanghai is important. The original market at Xiaodongmen had narrow wharves and incomplete storage facilities, which were not enough to supply the entire city with fish food, let alone supply the upstream of the Yangtze River with edible sea fish, which hinders the development of the fishing industry. Therefore, following the example of other countries, a fish market was built in Yangshupu, which is convenient for water transportation, using the latest equipment to seek the corresponding supply and demand of edible fish. On the one hand, methods are devised to provide relief to fishermen, and at the same time, in consideration of the old fish shops in Xiaodongmen, they are all given priority as brokers and invited to join. Not only are they prevented from losing their jobs, but they can also help them develop the fish market. However, the fish exchange is the same as other commodity exchanges. According to the fish market's business regulations, only the first transaction must be held in the fish market in order to freely and publicly auction, equalize fish prices, and avoid manipulation and hoarding, which would harm the interests of fishermen and consumers. After this, fish merchants can freely buy and sell in various places without restriction. The saying that it is unified control is naturally unfounded. Secondly, the rumor that tung oil is a monopoly is even more inconsistent with the facts. The purpose of the Ministry in establishing a vegetable oil plant is to cooperate with tung oil merchants to establish a company, with the intention of improving the quality of tung oil and establishing product standards, so that foreign businessmen who buy tung oil can benefit from good quality and factory prices. It does not restrict the freedom of Chinese and foreign merchants to buy and sell tung oil and does not contain the meaning of government controlling trade. In short, the Ministry hopes that the domestic agricultural, industrial, and commercial sectors can each establish a healthy body, and independently control and improve. If merchants and people lack the strength, the government is willing to cooperate with them to carry out the project, so that agriculture, industry, and commerce can adapt to the world's economic trends, unite and develop, and hold the goal of good quality and cheap prices to make up for the world's deficiencies with China's surplus. If all industries cannot unite and seek improvement, it is no longer what the times allow, and the government's responsibility is to promote its progress. The Ministry has always been determined to cooperate with merchants and people in various industries. Past undertakings have been like this, and future facilities will be no exception. (Central News Agency dispatch, 27th)

(Nanjing) An official of the Ministry of Industry said that the vegetable oil plant is starting preparations. Letters have been sent to hire Zhang Jiazhu, Deputy Director of the International Trade Bureau, and the directors of the construction departments of Hunan, Hubei, Sichuan, and Zhejiang provinces as preparatory committee members, with Zhang as the chairman. The chairmen and directors of the construction departments of the four provinces have been asked to quickly raise and recruit commercial shares for the share capital that each province should bear. The capital establishment meeting will be held by the end of next month. The first step in the plan is to set up a factory in Changsha, Hunan to refine tung oil, and set up a head office in Shanghai to be responsible for business and manage the affairs of various factories. The second step is to set up factories in Shanghai, Hankou, Changde, Wanxian, Chongqing, Hangzhou, Wenzhou, and other places as needed. The Ministry of Industry's share capital of 500,000 yuan has already allocated 250,000 yuan within the 24th year of the Republic budget (1935), and is also in contact with the Shanghai banking community to negotiate commercial shares of 250,000 yuan. (Special dispatch, 27th)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industry plans to establish a fisheries syndicate, with loans of 1 million yuan in the first year. The official shares of 100,000 yuan have been raised by the Ministry. As for the commercial shares of 800,000 yuan undertaken by the banking community, Wu Dingchang has made progress in negotiations in Shanghai. The location is attached to the fish market, and the establishment period is at the latest by the end of July. The capital will be increased to 2 million yuan in the second year, 3 million yuan in the third year, 4 million yuan in the fourth year, and 5 million yuan in the fifth year. (Special dispatch, 27th)

It is reported that the new contract, as amended, involves a loan of £1.1 million in British currency, with an annual interest rate of 6%, to be repaid within 25 years. The bonds will be underwritten by the Chinese-British Bank and the China Construction Bank. (27th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Key Points of the Fujian 25th Year Short-Term Treasury Bond Regulations 74

(Nanjing) The Fujian 25th Year Short-Term Provincial Treasury Bond Regulations were passed by the Executive Yuan meeting on the 26th. The key points are as follows:

* The total amount of treasury bonds is 900,000 yuan, divided into three denominations: 10,000 yuan, 1,000 yuan, and 100 yuan. They are issued in bearer form.

* The actual price received is 97 yuan.

* The bonds will be issued on November 1, 1936.

* The monthly interest rate is 7%.

* Repayment of principal and interest is guaranteed by the allocation of 50,000 yuan per month from the central subsidy and the remaining revenue from the provincial property and business tax, after deducting the funds earmarked for a portion of the Fujian Provincial Local Construction Public Bonds of the 24th Year of the Republic. The Fund Management Committee will deposit these funds with the Central Bank according to the listed amounts to cover the principal and interest payments when due.

* Repayment of principal will begin from the date of issuance. 10% of the principal will be repaid in each of the first four periods, and 12% of the principal will be repaid in each of the fifth through ninth periods. Principal and interest will be fully repaid by March 1937.

* The bonds can be mortgaged and traded, and can be used as security deposits for various public matters. Bonds that have reached their maturity date for principal and interest payments can be used to pay provincial taxes. (27th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Joint Sino-British Commission Conducted Survey of Yunnan-Burma Boundary 89

Liang Yugao Returns to Beijing to Report

Neutral Commissioner Advocates Fairness

Both Sides' Commissioners Express Satisfaction

Nanjing Dispatch: The Chinese and British governments previously sent commissioners to survey and demarcate the Yunnan-Burma border. Now, our Chinese commissioner, Liang Yugao, has returned to Beijing by Eurasia Aviation Corporation plane today to report. Liang Yugao made the following remarks to a reporter from the Kuomin News Agency:

"This joint survey of the southern section of the Yunnan-Burma boundary was conducted by two commissioners each from the Chinese and British governments, and one neutral commissioner dispatched by the League of Nations. We convened at the Yunnan-Burma border and conducted an on-site survey according to the treaty signed in 1897. All work of the survey commission was also predetermined by both governments with a 'Task Outline,' so that the work procedures and scope could be planned in a specific manner. I departed from Beijing at the end of September last year. After arriving in Kunming, I briefly liaised with the Yunnan provincial authorities and then proceeded overland to the meeting location, a journey of more than thirty days. On December 1st, according to the agreement between the two parties, I met with the neutral commissioner and the British commissioner at Hushan and began work. The British side was stationed at Jihu Shan, while our side was stationed at Nandai, about ten li away from Hushan. The British attendees were Chief Commissioner Clague, Commissioner Grose, and advisor Toller. Our attendees were Chief Commissioner Liang Yugao, Commissioner Yin Mingde, and Secretary-Director Li Liying. We held a total of thirty-three meetings there. Both sides presented witnesses and material evidence, and personally inspected relevant locations along the border line in order to resolve the first section of the boundary line. Afterward, we continuously moved to Jin Chang Ba (i.e., Lufang), Gang (i.e., near Ban Hong), Meng Jiao, Meng Dong, Laba, Lao Chang, and other places. On the one hand, we conducted on-site surveys of the boundary area. On the other hand, we held meetings with the British side to discuss various boundary line issues. By the time we were in Lao Chang, the Qingming Festival had passed, and miasma began to emerge with the rainy season. Coupled with continuous rain, surveying and demarcation work could not continue, so we decided to temporarily adjourn the meeting. In total, we held sixty-seven meetings. All personnel were in the deep mountains and wilderness, and all aspects of clothing, food, shelter, and transportation were very arduous. Furthermore, there were many local savages, ethnic minorities outside the pale of civilization, so the safety of the commission personnel could have been endangered at any time. Fortunately, the security team was very effective, and the Chinese staff were able to endure hardship and work calmly, so the boundary survey went quite smoothly. As for the head of the neutral commission, he was very fair and impartial for the sake of balance between the two countries. The British commissioners were also able to negotiate various issues in a spirit of friendship, as can be seen in the speeches of all parties at the closing of the meeting."

Closing Remarks of the Neutral Commissioner

"I would like to take this opportunity to thank the Chinese and British delegations for their surveyors and security teams, and to thank the commissioners of both sides for their spirit of cooperation."

Closing Remarks of Commissioner Liang

"Before the adjournment of this session, I propose that we formally thank the head of the neutral commission. During this time, the head of the neutral commission presided over all work of this meeting, fully utilizing his wisdom, spirit, and ability to lead this meeting. He was also able to judge the views of both sides with fairness and impartiality, which is very admirable to us. Moreover, his boundary work experience was of great assistance to this meeting. As for the areas that required on-site investigation, even though he fell from his horse and injured his foot, he was unwilling to lose even an hour of the meeting's time due to his personal injury. He personally went to the high mountains and steep ridges with his injury to conduct field surveys and investigations, striving to clarify the truth as the basis for his judgment. He did not omit a single word of the work stipulated in the "Task Outline" established by the two governments. This spirit of dedicated service is also worthy of our admiration. Of course, we often had different views from the head of the neutral commission on various issues. When we reached these different views, I knew that his judgment was based on his own conscience and his own beliefs. I hope that the head of the neutral commission will be able to come and guide us again when we continue our work next time. In addition to proposing a formal thank you to the head of the neutral commission, I would also like to record the pleasure of working with the British commissioners this time. Of course, we also had different views, but in the midst of these different views, we were often able to understand each other's difficulties. I hope that the work of our two parties can help our governments to resolve this decades-long pending case and further the friendship between the two great powers."

Closing Remarks of Clague

"I very much agree with Commissioner Liang's opinion. The head of the neutral commission's experience in boundary affairs can indeed provide us with extremely valuable assistance. This section of the boundary line was left unresolved by General Liu and Scoggs twenty-six years ago. We hope to resolve this issue based on the boundary experience of the head of the neutral commission. Commissioner Liang also said that the head of the neutral commission's judgment is based entirely on conscience. I am very happy to second Commissioner Liang's proposal. I am also very grateful to the Chinese delegation for the various assistance they provided to us when we passed through various parts of China, especially the assistance that our surveying team and food transport team received in the South, which was even more valuable. I feel very happy to work with Commissioner Liang Yugao and others this time. I wish the head of the neutral commission and the Chinese commissioner a safe journey back."

North China Smuggling Difficulties

Concerns Remain Regarding New Anti-Smuggling Measures

Japanese Side Still Wants to Reduce Tariffs

Tianjin Dispatch: The Central Government has recently promulgated the North China Anti-Smuggling Regulations, which the Tianjin Customs has successively received. However, there are many obstacles to implementation. Furthermore, because the assistance of railway authorities is needed, the Jinpu Railway was directly ordered by the Ministry of Railways to set up tax checkpoints at stations and inspection offices along the line, and customs officers boarded trains to inspect passengers. This was not a problem. Only the Beining Railway Bureau, under pressure from foreign forces, had more concerns and was unwilling to immediately comply with the Ministry's order. In terms of diplomacy, the Jicha Political Affairs Commission previously instructed Xiao Zhenying to be responsible for negotiations with the Japanese side. The Japanese military and the Japanese consulate expressed a unified focus on reducing tariffs. They stated that if another preferential tariff treaty for North China were concluded, smugglers would have no profit to gain, and smuggling would cease on its own. Xiao once relayed this idea to the Ministry of Finance and the Jicha Political Affairs Commission. However, the Central Government has indirectly made it clear that reducing tariffs is impossible. Therefore, diplomatically speaking, there is currently no solution. The Beining Railway Bureau is also using this as an excuse to shirk responsibility and delay, intending to evade the issue. Xu Liya, the Tianjin Customs Commissioner, and Sipu, the Anti-Smuggling Commissioner, have repeatedly contacted Lin Shize, the Customs Superintendent, and representatives of the Beining Railway Bureau, seeking to study a peaceful and appropriate solution within the new central law. As a result, no new decision has been reached. Because of the repeated urging of the customs, the Beining Railway Bureau has begun to consult with the Ministry of Railways and the Jicha Political Affairs Commission, waiting for a reply before making a decision. However, this is not a time when the authorities have the power to make a firm decision. The reply will not arrive in the end, and the Beining Railway Bureau will not provide substantial assistance in the end. Because of the difficulty in strictly suppressing smuggling, the Customs is currently only rectifying matters within its own scope. A few days ago, it specifically ordered customs officers not to neglect their duties or collude with vagrants to harbor smuggling. Otherwise, severe punishment will be imposed when discovered. Although this is close to empty words, it is quite necessary at this time.

In recent months, due to the excessive smuggling of sugar, the sales of domestic sugar have been almost completely seized. Traditionally, domestic sugar in Tianjin is divided into Fujian, Chaozhou, and Shantou factions, with more than 100 wholesale shops in total. The peak season for goods is in spring and autumn, shipped by Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, and China Merchants Steam Navigation Company vessels. Sales in the three provinces of Chahar, Suiyuan, and Shanxi also use Tianjin as a transit point. The annual arrival of goods is about 50 million bags. From this spring to the present, it has gradually become a situation where there are goods but no market. Statistics show that less than 500,000 bags have arrived. In the past, each bag of 100 catties sold for 18 yuan, but now it sells for 10 yuan. Even with a price drop of 8 yuan, few people are interested. Smuggled sugar currently sells for 5 yuan per 100 catties. Compared to this, domestic sugar is twice as expensive, so buyers naturally abandon this and choose that. Therefore, from March to the present, more than 70 of the 100 or so wholesale shops have closed down, and only 30 or so are barely supporting themselves. They have also sent telegrams to their headquarters in Fujian, Chaozhou, and Shantou, stopping the arrival of goods. If smuggling continues to be so rampant, these 30 or so shops will probably be unable to maintain themselves in three months.

According to customs investigations, the smuggling of rayon was most prevalent from February to late April, with a total of 4.78 million pieces transported. Imports were fewer in May, with about 500,000 pieces. In total, about 6.3 million pieces were transported in three months. The number of pieces sold, on average, in April, was 500,000 to 600,000 pieces in Zhoucun, Shandong Province, 300,000 pieces in Gaoyang, Hebei Province, 300,000 to 400,000 pieces in Tianjin, 50,000 to 100,000 pieces in Beiping and its suburbs, and 21,000 pieces in Shanghai. In total, 1.2 million pieces were sold in two months. The remaining approximately 3 million pieces can still be sold for two months based on previous figures. Currently, it is the off-season for rayon sales. If they are to be completely sold out, it will be around the end of July. Therefore, various goods are stockpiled in Tianjin and cannot be sold off for the time being. Smugglers have had to change their plans and seek other options. The increasing imports and strong sales of petroleum are one proof of this. It is said that in half a month, 20,000 boxes were transported from the pseudo-Jidong region to Tianjin. 6,000 boxes remain in Nandasi and Beidaihe. The selling price per box in Tianjin has risen from more than 6 yuan to 7.2 yuan, which is more than 1 yuan cheaper than Mobil and Asiatic kerosene. The goods are sold as soon as they arrive, and there is a situation of demand exceeding supply. The selling price of Dalian kerosene per box is 3.7 yuan. Adding transportation costs, the cost of smuggled goods to Tianjin is 4.8 yuan, with a net profit of more than 1.4 yuan. Smugglers are constantly on the road. At the same time, British and American oil merchants are also feeling the greatest panic.

According to shipping industry sources, since March of this year, the transport of smuggled goods has been booming, and legitimate shipping companies have been affected. Because vagrant goods are mostly transported by civilian ships or steamships, or sometimes transported by Japanese ships, the domestic shipping companies operating on the Yingkou, Dalian, and Andong lines have had to reduce their ship schedules in order to reduce losses. Furthermore, the Tianjin-Yingkou route is restricted by the puppet Manchukuo. Ships sailing to Yingkou must be registered with the puppet Ministry of Transportation and recognized as having Manchukuo nationality, otherwise they are only allowed to load legitimate cargo, and even passengers are not allowed to be carried. This year, there are more passengers leaving the customs than in previous years, and passenger fares are very high. Domestic shipping companies had intended to rely on this to supplement their revenue, but they have been restricted. The future of their business is very worrying. (25th)

Songjiang: County Magistrate Li Streamlines Cases of Opium Offenders 90

The county prison is overcrowded with opium offenders. Several have died of illness. A provincial order to streamline cases was previously received, but the actual situation has not been addressed. County Magistrate Li, seeing this situation, felt compassionate and, at 8:00 a.m. yesterday, accompanied by staff members Zhu Rongli, Section Chief Feng, Bureau Chief He, and Secretary Shen, brought case files and personally went to the prison to summon each detained opium offender for detailed questioning in order to distinguish and streamline cases and avoid innocent people being implicated. At the same time, he instructed prison officials to quickly open several new cells to be places for treating sick opium offenders. The questioning was completed at 12:00 p.m. and he will select minor offenders for parole. At 1:00 p.m., he gathered representatives from various hospitals to discuss improving the prison's sanitation facilities and accompanied the doctors to inspect the prison and provide free treatment to sick inmates. However, it is feared that the poor without guarantors will still inevitably become wronged souls in the black registers.

Kunshan: Baijia Village Robbery Case 92

Baijia Village, in the Luzhi Bang Township of the third district of Kunshan County, located near the Wusong River, was robbed at approximately 12:00 p.m. on the 26th. They looted a considerable amount of jewelry, rice, clothing, and other items, worth approximately over a thousand yuan. After about three hours, the bandits fled towards the Wusong River. Afterwards, the victims, fearing revenge from the bandits, did not report the case to the county to request an arrest.

Suzhou: Impersonating Anti-Smuggling to Rob Boats 94

Amidst the reports of smuggling in North China, the term "anti-smuggling" has repeatedly appeared in the news. Unexpectedly, anti-smuggling has not yet been effectively implemented, but armed robberies have already occurred at the border between Wuxian and Wujiang counties under the guise of "anti-smuggling." It is reported that Ms. Wu Zhiqing, a female employee working at the Wujiang Farmers Bank, traveled by boat with her mother, female servant from Suzhou to Pingwang, her original home, on the 26th. When the boat passed near Yinshan Bridge at the border between Wuxian and Wujiang counties, a group of people (several of whom were armed), resembling public officials and wearing badges, suddenly appeared, claiming to be ordered to conduct anti-smuggling operations and ordered the boat to stop for inspection. The boat immediately docked. The men boarded the boat and carried out a search, but found no prohibited items. They then robbed about over a hundred yuan in gold jewelry and silver dollars. At the same time, they also inspected several other passing boats, but found nothing. After about an hour, they allowed Wu Zhiqing's boat to leave, and the men disappeared. Afterwards, Wu Zhiqing realized that they were impersonating officials to rob. Upon arriving in Wujiang, she reported the incident to the local water and land police. Zhou Weilie, the water police district chief, upon receiving the report from the Wujiang detachment on the 27th, in addition to strictly investigating, also dispatched patrol boats to patrol the Yinshan and Guoxiang area to prevent accidents and maintain water security.

Request for Investigation of Embezzlement of Public Funds Case 95

Zhu Jingbo, the former director of the Wuxian County Land Tax Collection Office, was accused of corruption. After a thorough investigation by officials dispatched by the Ministry of Finance, it was confirmed that there were indeed corrupt practices. He has been ordered to hand over 18,000 yuan, the proceeds of his corruption from the "Disaster Relief Item" of the 21st year. Now, the Ministry of Finance, considering that Zhu has been in office for eight years, in addition to the 21st year which has been investigated, there are other years when he handled "Mangcao" (grain transportation); whether there are any corrupt practices has not yet been investigated. Therefore, it has ordered the county to continue to investigate in detail and report, so that it can be verified and handled. Recently, it was discovered that Cha Yueshou, a senior official in Wujing, is Zhu Jingbo's prison brother-in-law. Taking advantage of his power, he and Zhu jointly embezzled several thousands of dollars in accumulated rent from the public land of the Cangchu Si, which was managed by Cha. There is also suspicion of illegally selling public land and houses. Many of the initiators who purchased the public land, such as Yu and Wang, submitted a petition to the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Supervisory Office on the 27th, requesting a thorough investigation to clarify the truth.

Thorough Investigation of Judicial Officer Feces-Splashing Case 97

Liu Rongshan, a judge who was temporarily acting as the presiding judge of the criminal court of the Wuxi District Court, was walking from Mianhua Lane outside the West Gate to the court to work on the morning of the 21st, when suddenly a young thug came up to him in the West Drum Tower Alley and splashed feces on Judge Liu's face, covering him from head to toe. The thug then calmly fled. Afterwards, the case was reported to the prosecutor's office, and Qian Zhengxiang and Fan, who were suspected of committing the crime, were detained. According to their confession, they were instigated by a lawyer named Sun. Yesterday morning, warrants were signed to order the police to summon Sun and others for questioning. Yangzhou: Two Riverboats Robbed at Loujin Town 98

The Zhenhuai class small boat of the Fu Yun Company, departed from Huai at around 11:00 p.m. on the 25th. When traveling through Loujin Town, it was suddenly attacked by multiple bandits who boarded the boat to rob. At the same time, the Qingzhen class boat of the Zhengtong Xiajia Company, which had departed from Qing, was also robbed in the town. In addition, several pig boats had several fat pigs stolen by bandits.

Pork Industry Suspends Operations and Raises Prices 99

The pork business in the county has two kinds of taxes: the slaughter tax and the meat donation. Since the establishment of the Donation and Tax Management Committee, the meat donation has been considered harsh and petty, and it was abolished by provincial order. Recently, the Ministry of Finance, based on the Ministry's order, stated that the slaughter tax refers to the entire pig. If it is sold to the workshops and markets, and retailed in pieces, this is called commercial operation, and business tax should be paid according to the percentage regulations for other goods. Director Jin of the County Business Tax Bureau, after receiving the order, first gathered the pork merchants in the city and suburbs to inquire about the amount of each business turnover and determine the lightness or heaviness of the tax rate. At first, the pork merchants did not have any objections. Afterwards, they suddenly unanimously opposed it and, starting on the 26th, agreed to suspend operations for three days as a form of resistance. Each pork stall posted a rectangular strip that read: "Pork prices are high, business losses, operations suspended for three days, public discussion to raise prices." In order to resolve the situation, it is heard that the matter will ultimately be resolved by raising prices.

Ningbo: Fire at Dongdu Road 100

The Wuchang Hat Shop on Dongdu Road in this port, has been open for more than thirty years and its business has been decent. Unexpectedly, a fire broke out suddenly at around 1:00 a.m. this morning. The shop's employees all escaped from their sleep. The fire was put out after about half an hour after various firefighters arrived. One three-story building was destroyed, and two three-story empty buildings next to it, belonging to Shuangfengxiang, were also slightly affected. The loss is estimated at about five or six thousand dollars. It is heard that the cause of the fire was an electrical short circuit.

Nantong: Smuggling Case Submitted to Province for Disposition 101

The case involved four unlicensed Japanese men, including Yamasaki, who are still being guarded by police in Room 52 of the Chonghai Hotel. Chu, a military judge of the Commissioner's Office, went to the hotel at 4:00 p.m. to question Yamasaki and others. Whether to send them to the province or not will be decided after receiving a reply from the provincial government.

Bengbu: Twists and Turns of the Small Loan 102

The amount of the small loan program for the banking industry here was originally set at 190,000 yuan. Afterwards, borrowers were enthusiastic, and the amount of the loan exceeded the budget, so that it was not possible to provide universal relief. In addition, the number of households that were disqualified due to unqualified inspections or guarantee problems was as high as 104, which was quite dissatisfactory to all industries. Representatives from various industries have been negotiating with Yu, a member of the Guarantee and Credit Committee, for days, asking the Guarantee and Credit Committee to temporarily refrain from lending to borrowers who have already been approved for loans by the banking industry, and to process the cases of those who are guaranteeing and those who have been disqualified first, and then release the funds at the same time. Otherwise, the release of funds will be stopped. According to the person in charge of the Chamber of Commerce, if the disqualified households do not have guarantees, the entire committee is willing to provide financial guarantee. Furthermore, the Chamber of Commerce, believing that the small loan of 30,000 yuan is not enough to lend, contacted the banking industry to request an additional loan of 20,000 yuan for distribution. On the 26th, all the executive and supervisory committee members of the Chamber of Commerce jointly sent a letter to the banking industry association, requesting that loans be provided to all industry households to avoid discrimination and cause disputes.

Reading of the Eulogy

"On the twelfth day of the fifth month of the twenty-fifth year of the Republic of China, Hu Gong Zhantang, Chairman of the Central Executive Committee, passed away in Guangdong due to illness. Upon receiving the news in Shanghai, all our countrymen were filled with grief. Tracing back to the late Qing Dynasty, foreign invasions were frequent, and the people suffered greatly. The Aisin Gioro clan enslaved our Han Chinese, intensifying their oppression. With his extraordinary talent, Gong embarked on the path of martial prowess, assisting Premier Sun in his travels abroad, rallying comrades, loudly proclaiming, and promoting revolution. In numerous uprisings, Gong participated in the planning and execution. Although facing repeated failures, Gong's determination never wavered. In the Revolution of 1911, the Manchu dynasty was overthrown, and the Republic was established. Gong's contribution was paramount. Gong then relinquished honor and privilege, retiring after achieving success. Alas, Heaven did not favor China. First, Yuan Shikai usurped power, and the imperial system was revived. Then, warlords carved up the country, causing widespread suffering. Public indignation grew, and Gong once again followed Premier Sun, engaging in revolution. After the success of the Northern Expedition, Gong held key positions, but eventually, due to the strain on his health, he retired to the south, embarking on a long voyage, hoping to rest and prolong his years. However, the national crisis deepened daily, and the central government relied heavily on him. Gong, adhering to his original intention of sacrificing himself to save the country, had no choice but to return and shoulder heavy responsibilities. How could we have foreseen that Heaven would not grant him long life, and his fortune would be cut short? A great man has fallen, and a pillar has collapsed. Alas, alas! Our Shanghai public organizations, upon receiving orders, convened a memorial meeting on May 25th. We, being among the last to participate, deeply moved by his merits and virtues, offer this eulogy, saying: How sad that illness could not be overcome, that a pillar of the nation has fallen and Gong has departed! As the state of the nation deteriorates daily, who will offer solutions? Heaven has not left us an heir, and our hearts are filled with sorrow. Born a hero, may your spirit rest in peace. Bless our country and benefit our people. If the netherworld can be stirred, it will be moved by our words. Alas, alas!" Respectfully eulogized by all directors and supervisors of the Shanghai Municipal Education Association.

Customs Brokers' Union Requests Elimination of Transit Tax 105

The Shanghai Customs Brokers' Association submitted a report to the Ministry of Transportation yesterday, stating: "The customs brokerage industry relies entirely on transportation, and the key to transportation lies in shipping. Therefore, the prosperity of the customs brokerage industry is always seen as dependent on the success or failure of the shipping industry. Although the businesses are different, the relationship is extremely close, with only direct and indirect connections being the difference. Since the Ministry implemented combined water and land transportation, shipping of goods by ship has gradually decreased. The reason for this is that goods transported by private boats, railways, and postal packages, whether to inland ports or treaty ports, are uniformly tax-exempt with government approval. However, goods transported by ships are only exempt from taxes when traveling from inland areas to treaty ports. For goods transported between treaty ports, transit taxes must still be paid. As a result, in order to avoid transit taxes and reduce costs, both cargo and passengers reject ships and opt for trains, sailboats, or postal services. Consequently, ship cargo has decreased, and our industry is also declining. Your Ministry is promoting the transportation industry, and ships, railways, postal services, and private boats should all be taken into consideration. However, national tax revenue should be reformed, and uniform treatment should be given. At a time when the circulation and transportation of domestic products are being promoted, shipping taxes should be exempted. Otherwise, the cargo of ships will decline further, and our government will inevitably overlook this and lose that, which is lacking in the purpose of emphasizing both water and land transportation. Moreover, the domestic railway development is not yet complete. The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway has already opened to traffic, and the Guangdong-Hankou Railway is about to be completed. In the future, railways and highways will be accessible in all directions. If the transit tax is not abolished quickly, ship cargo will inevitably disappear. With the failure of shipping, the vitality of our industry will also be exhausted. Recently, it has been heard that the shipping industry has repeatedly appealed to your Ministry and the Ministry of Finance. Although permission has been granted for abolition, no clear implementation order has been seen. Our industry is extremely anxious for the sake of livelihood and future prospects. Member associations have repeatedly requested the elimination of transit taxes, hoping for early implementation to make up for the losses. Therefore, we dare to report the situation and earnestly request you to quickly urge the Ministry of Finance to issue a clear order for abolition, so as to equalize treatment and alleviate business difficulties. We await your orders with trepidation. Sincerely, Chen Panjun, Standing Committee Member and Chairman of the Shanghai Shipping and Customs Brokers' Association."

French Silk Industry Association Requests Implementation of Raw Silk Grading and Inspection; Ministry of Industry and Commerce Orders the Bureau of Inspection and Testing to Prepare 106

The export of raw silk from our country is equally important to France and the United States. As proof, the output of Shanghai silk factories to France and the United States was 20,000 packages each last year. However, in the past, sales in France were greater than in the United States. In recent years, due to competition from Japanese silk in France, Chinese silk has plummeted in value. The prices of Japanese silk and Chinese silk are similar, but because Japanese silk is of uniform quality and convenient to purchase, it surpasses Chinese silk. Yesterday, the Shanghai Raw Silk Exporters' Association received a letter from the Lyon Silk Industry Association of France, stating that France has always welcomed Chinese silk, and general weaving houses are very willing to purchase it. However, in recent years, Japanese silk has encroached on the Chinese silk market, and sales of Chinese silk in France have decreased year by year. Although there are many reasons for this, the main one is that the Japanese government has formulated grades and conducted strict inspections. Therefore, the quality of Japanese silk is uniform and unified, making transactions very convenient in the French market. When purchasing Japanese silk, it is not necessary to ask about the brand name. It is only a way to identify a batch of raw silk, not a standard for its grade. Therefore, this association specifically writes to your association, requesting the Chinese government to formulate Chinese silk grades and stipulate quality standards for each grade. These standards must be similar to those of Japanese silk, so that France can still compete to purchase Chinese silk, and the French market will not be completely seized by Japan. In addition, the raw silk cohesion test should be implemented in accordance with the methods of the Japanese inspection agency by the Chinese government inspection agency. It is heard that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has ordered the Shanghai Commodity Inspection and Testing Bureau to prepare for the implementation of raw silk grading and inspection. It is expected that it will be opened around the autumn of this year, which is truly good news for the foreign trade of raw silk.

New Life Movement Association Requests Organization of Labor Service Corps, Creating the Foundation of Modern National Obligatory Labor; Establishment Required Within One Month, Service to Commence Two Weeks Later 107

The Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association, holding labor as life's duty and service as life's vocation, organized Youth Service Corps at the beginning of the New Life Movement to carry out labor service in various districts on weekends and to persuade citizens to practice the New Life Movement, which achieved considerable results. However, in the past, the members of the organization were mostly local teams of students and youths, which was considered insufficient to promote the entire society and all sectors. Therefore, at the last executive committee meeting, in accordance with the regulations of the General Association, three kinds of "Regulations for the Shanghai Municipal Organs, Schools, and Social Organizations to Organize New Life Labor Service Corps" were formulated (the original Youth Service Corps will not be abolished for the time being), and the focus and purpose of its work were defined. This was intended to inform the public to take the lead, sparing no effort, and then to organize and educate the people in order to support public morale, improve society, and create the foundation of modern national obligatory labor. It is reported that the association has yesterday sent the above regulations, along with application charts and attachments, to various organs in the city and instructed its affiliated organs, middle schools, and social organizations, etc., to be informed and prepare in accordance with the regulations, that is, to complete the organization and establishment within one month and start service two weeks later. Any organs, schools, and social organizations in remote areas or working outside the city, if they have not received the notification and feel the need, can request a supplementary copy from their respective administrative organs or directly from the New Life Movement Association in Fenglin Bridge.

Page 10

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Notifies All Industries to Actively Report Smuggled Goods 108

Based on the Authority Granted by the Government, All Guilds Must Pay Close Attention

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce issued a notice to all industry guilds yesterday regarding the prevention of the circulation of smuggled goods, stating that the Chamber had previously noted that smuggling in North China had a significant impact on merchants in the city and had issued letters to related industries to solicit prevention measures. Subsequently, it received replies from the cotton cloth industry and the woolen industry, which were forwarded to the Ministry of Finance for adoption. On the 26th of this month, it also received a letter from the Silk and Satin Industry Association stating that the industry was severely affected by smuggling in North China, especially artificial silk fabrics and artificial silk interwoven fabrics, with the most significant price differences. For example, the cost of smuggled dull silk per yard is less than twenty cents, while the cost of manufacturing in China is more than forty cents per yard. This is just one example, and the rest can be inferred. The price of each box of rayon in Japan is about one hundred yuan, while smuggled goods in North China are sold for only one hundred and seventy yuan. However, legally taxed goods in Shanghai need to pay more than two hundred and eighty yuan in taxes per box, plus a cost of one hundred yuan, so each box has to be sold for more than three hundred and eighty yuan. Therefore, the cost of raw materials differs by more than one time, resulting in the prevalence of smuggled goods. If no urgent measures are taken, domestic silk factories will face the risk of suspending production. Therefore, the association convened a temporary emergency meeting to discuss. It was generally agreed that effective ways to stop smuggling, before the central government protests have been made and stopped it, besides the severe cooperation from everywhere, should include a request to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to persuade all industries to monitor each other and refuse to purchase smuggled goods. If any secret purchases are discovered with concrete evidence, they should be secretly reported to the government for severe punishment, so that a warning can be given as a deterrent to those who seek illicit profits. The decision was made to reply to the letter accordingly. Now, due to the previous reasons, the impact of smuggling and the association’s views are presented in a letter. The Interim Regulations on the Inspection of Imported Goods and Transportation have been promulgated by the government. According to Article 17 of the regulations, all industry guilds are responsible for reporting tax evasion and smuggled goods and are entitled to rewards. The Silk and Satin Industry Association's so-called monitoring and secret reporting are already stipulated in the Interim Regulations. As a group of legitimate merchants, each guild should pay close attention to this rampant smuggling, which is a matter of vital interest, and act in accordance with the authority granted by the government, report the facts truthfully at any time, and help the country's economy and people's livelihood from deteriorating. Do not give up slightly, this is our hope.

Tea Exports Suddenly Suffer Setback; Opening Extended to Friday 109

Two Measures Proposed by Foreign Merchants

Marketing Office Has Responded

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, after the Qimen black tea samples were distributed to foreign firms by the Marketing Office, the foreign firms convened their colleagues to evaluate the tea. The original plan was to open the market for trading this Monday, but it was later rescheduled to 9:00 a.m. yesterday. Unexpectedly, the foreign merchants suddenly proposed two conditions yesterday morning: 1. The Marketing Office must find a bank to guarantee that the tea transaction is successful and that the goods match the samples; 2. The Marketing Office must specify the intermediaries for transactions with tea merchants. As a result, a setback occurred, and the opening was suddenly suspended. It is reported that the Marketing Office has now responded to these two measures. First, the Marketing Office will find the Bank of Communications to provide a guarantee for the goods worth less than 100,000, and stipulate that if any discrepancies are found between the goods and samples within eight months after the transaction is successful, the guarantor will compensate or refund the price. The second measure is currently being selected, and both parties have agreed to open the market this Friday (the 29th) without further delay. It is expected that the implementation of tea transactions will open a new situation. It is also learned that foreign tea merchants are now expressing their willingness to cooperate sincerely with the Marketing Office. Hong Mengpan, chairman of the Tea Industry Association, and Chen Yizhou, manager of Zhongxin Chang, are willing to cooperate to jointly plan methods to promote tea sales.

Customs Revises Rules for Vessels' Import Manifests 111

Article 3, Item E

Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Barenson, Commissioner of Customs, specially issued a joint proclamation on the revision of Article 3, Item E of the Rules for Vessels' Import and Export Manifests: It is hereby announced that the Rules for Vessels' Import and Export Manifests have been posted in the Customs Notice No. 1384. It is now ordered by the Ministry of Finance to revise Article 3 (E) of the aforementioned Rules as follows: (E) If a vessel imports from overseas, in addition to detailing the above four items (A, B, C, and D) in the hatch list, the weight and dimensions of each piece of cargo on board should be detailed, and the names of each consignee should be entered in the hatch list according to the bill of lading or package receipt. If the name of the consignee is not listed in the bill of lading or receipt, it should also be noted in the hatch list. However, if the shipping manifest prepared at the foreign port of shipment lists the weight and dimensions of each piece of cargo, this shipping manifest may be attached to the hatch list to avoid separate filling. All merchants are hereby notified.

Japanese Merchants Plan to Establish a Goods Market 112

Organization Similar to an Exchange

Ministry of Finance Cables Shanghai Municipal Government to Investigate and Reply

According to the New Voice News Agency, there are currently five exchanges in Shanghai: the Chinese Merchants' Cotton Yarn Exchange, the Chinese Merchants' Securities Exchange, the Grain Exchange, the Gold Exchange, and the Flour Exchange. The Ministry of Finance has sent supervisors to oversee the operations of each exchange. Now, Japanese merchants in Shanghai are planning to establish a goods exchange in Shanghai (i.e., a trading center) that includes cotton yarn, grains, flour, etc., under the name of "Shanghai Goods Market" and registered with the Japanese Consulate-General in Shanghai. In reality, it is a disguised exchange with a preparation office located at No. 15, Route des Soeurs.

All Sectors Pay Attention

The Cotton Yarn, Grain, and Flour Exchanges, as well as various industrial sectors, are paying close attention to the event of Japanese merchants establishing a goods market. They believe that if the goods market is a disguised exchange, it should be banned by law. However, before the contents of the market's operations are formally announced, they have not yet expressed their views. A Nanjing telegram stated that the Chinese Merchants' Cotton Yarn Exchange has telegraphed the Ministries of Finance and Industry to seek ways to prevent it. According to Mr. Mu Ouchu, the chairman of the Exchange, what the newspaper wrote is not factual.

Ministry Orders Investigation and Reply

The Ministry of Finance, upon receiving reports that Japanese merchants are planning to organize a goods exchange in Shanghai, specially telegraphed the Shanghai Municipal Government to quickly investigate and report back for review. The goods market has established a preparation office and is currently actively preparing. The persons in charge are Chinese citizens, Lu Zhisheng and Tan Haiqiu. However, according to Tan and Lu, who spoke to reporters from the New Voice News Agency, the organizers are Japanese merchants residing in Shanghai, and they are only assisting on their behalf.

Jiangyu Steamer Ran Aground Downstream of Huangshigang 113

Stranded Due to Rising Water and Heavy Fog

Construction-Aid Ships Sent and Military Police Dispatched

The Jiangyu, a steamer of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, with a deadweight of 3,084 tons, a registered tonnage of 2,262 tons, a length of 300 feet, a width of 42 feet 3 inches, a draft of blank 　feet, a loaded draft of 11 feet 8 inches, a horsepower of 1,750, and a speed of 12 knots per hour, has a cargo hold capacity of 116,012 cubic feet. It has 10 first-class cabins, 32 second-class cabins, 96 second-class berths, 178 third-class berths, and unlimited open berths. It was built in 1883. It departed on the afternoon of the 26th and arrived above Jiujiang at

Downstream of Huangshigang

Two nautical miles away, it encountered heavy fog, making it difficult to distinguish the river surface. Recently, with the rising water, the shallow banks along the river have also been submerged, making it even harder to recognize. Due to the negligence of the pilot, it mistakenly entered the area and ran aground suddenly. The shipowner, Huang Honglai, wanted to reverse to get out of the shoal, but he was unable to do so, so he sent a telegram to

Shanghai and Hankou for Help

The Hankou branch received the report and immediately planned to send the Lijie steamer to rescue it. At the same time, it telegraphed the Shanghai headquarters, stating that the Jiangyu steamer was stranded in a very bad location, and the ship was stuck in the shoal, making the situation very dangerous. It urgently requested that all steamers navigating upstream and downstream of the river provide assistance. Currently, the Jianguo steamer has gone to tow it. Moreover, the area is a troubled area with bandits, making the Jiangyu's grounding even more dangerous. The Hankou branch has requested that local armed military police be sent to the area to protect the ship to prevent accidents, while rescue operations are underway. The headquarters, upon receiving the report, telegraphed the Hankou and Xunyang branches and all Yangtze River steamers yesterday afternoon to find ways to assist in the rescue. It is noted that there were no passengers on board the Jiangyu steamer.

Special Trade Unions Vigorously Fight for the Right to Elect National Representatives 115

Postal Workers' Federation

The National Postal Workers' Federation telegraphed the Central Government yesterday to request the Central Government to increase the number of representatives of special trade unions to the National Assembly. The telegram stated: "To the Nanjing Central Executive Committee, the Department of Mass Training, the Executive Yuan, and the Legislative Yuan: We are deeply disturbed that the annex to the National Assembly Representative Election Law passed by the Legislative Yuan does not include representatives from the special trade unions of postal, telecommunications, railway, and maritime workers. According to Article 19 of the Election Law, our special trade unions of postal, telecommunications, railway, and maritime workers have not been listed among the professional groups because the government has not yet promulgated special trade union laws that meet practical needs. However, the associations of special trade unions are spread throughout the country, with a large number of members, and they all have a glorious history and sound organization. The National Assembly Representative Election issue is related to the vital interests of hundreds of thousands of people. It seems that we cannot rashly disregard the facts, deprive them of their rights, and exclude them. Therefore, in the National Assembly Representative Election Law, our special trade unions of postal, telecommunications, railway, and maritime workers should be recognized as legitimate professional groups, each with the right to participate in the election of representatives. Secondly, the professional elections stipulated in the National Assembly Representative Election Law are not only subject to regional restrictions, but also only divide the professional categories into three types of representatives: agriculture, industry, and commerce, and the number is extremely small. Taking the trade union item as an example, in the Shanghai area alone, there are hundreds of professional categories, and the purposes and interests of each industry are different. If the regulations of the election law are followed, the representatives produced, although nominally professional representatives, cannot actually represent any profession. If the members of special trade unions such as postal, telecommunications, railway, and maritime workers are engaged in a national unified professional with their own special interests and purposes, they should not participate in the professional elections which are only nominally there, and should request that each special trade union such as postal, telecommunications, railway, and maritime workers be an election unit, not subject to regional restrictions, and the number of representatives should be determined according to the proportion of the number of people, so as to implement the spirit of the professional representative system, and that is beneficial to the country. It concerns the rights of hundreds of thousands of transport workers, so it is requested to review and approve it, and quickly order it to be revised and implemented, which is really convenient. National Postal Workers' Federation Koushou, Gan."

Maritime and Land Party Workers

The Special Party Department of the Chinese Seamen's Union, the Chinese Seamen's Union, the Special Party Department of the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, and the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Workers' Union jointly petitioned the Standing Committee of the Central Committee, the Central Organization Department, and the Central Department of Mass Training to increase the number of representatives from various special trade unions to the National Assembly. The original presentation is recorded below: "The case of increasing the number of representatives from special trade unions to the National Assembly has been previously presented to your association (department) by our party department and union, as well as the Special Party Department of the Pinghan Railway. Now, our party department and union, due to the frequent letters and telegrams from various seamen's and railway workers' groups, and many representatives have been sent to appeal, requesting to send personnel to lead them to the capital to petition your association (department) and the National Government to fight for the issue of the number of national representatives of special trade unions. Considering the urgency of the situation, and not yet receiving the definite measures of the instructions from your association (department), on the 22nd of this month, a joint symposium of the party departments of various special trade unions was held at the Chinese Seamen's Union. It was decided that 'representatives of the party departments and unions of seamen and railway workers across the country will be jointly organized to go to Beijing on a regular basis to petition your association (department) and the National Government to increase the number of representatives of special trade unions to the National Assembly, and the various agencies present will jointly submit to your association (department) first,' etc., are recorded. The case involves the political power of most workers and the legislative plan of the Party and the country, which is very important. According to the principle of the National Assembly Representative Election Law decided by your association (department) in the past, the fourth principle of 'professional groups take the group as the unit, without dividing into regions, and the distribution of the number is based on the number of members or business　standards,' and the recently promulgated annex to the National Representative Election Law, the trade unions are divided into provincial and municipal regions. Compared to the two, there are obvious discrepancies, disregarding our special trade unions with millions of transport workers. Whether in the principles of the law, the equal status of civil rights, and the legislative procedures of the central principles, it is not fair. Therefore, the workers are complaining and feeling really sympathetic. Furthermore, in terms of the indivisible integrity of the special trade unions and the mobility of members, it is indeed inconvenient to participate in the elections of several provinces and cities or to participate in the elections of a certain province and city as a whole. Moreover, the Election Law does not have any clear provisions on how our special trade unions should participate in the elections. Our central government has always attached importance to professional groups, especially our special trade unions, and is particularly concerned about them, so it is placed under the direct jurisdiction of the Party, and there is no reason to discriminate. The omissions and errors of the Legislative Yuan this time should be that the Ministry of Industry, based on the relationship of jurisdiction, did not pay attention to the professional groups directly under the Central Committee or special party departments. The village materials provided to the Legislative Yuan were already omitted, and the legislative gentlemen did not have time to make reference in a hurry, so this kind of error occurred. In summary, the mistakes, omissions, and obstacles that have already occurred in terms of principles, legislative principles and procedures, and practical difficulties should be amended according to the previous first column of revisions of the civil and criminal laws, and ask for the approval to present to the Standing Committee and to re-allocate the number of national representatives of our special trade unions according to the pre-ordered proportion in light of the expectations of millions of transport workers, so that it is absolutely impossible to make the excuse that the law 　has already been promulgated, causing most of our workers to lose political power. The urgent statement leaves no time to choose. In addition to presenting separately, I hope you will carefully examine and quickly approve it for the convenience of the Party."

Seafarers Branch

Seafarers and railways, various special trade unions, regarding the issue of requesting to increase the number of representatives to the National Assembly, have been vying to fight for the various situations from the government in recent days, all of which are recorded in previous newspapers.
