The Reading Movement of the Past Year 191

— He Hanguang

The superficiality of academic atmosphere in our country cannot be denied by anyone. And the number of domestic cultural organizations devoted to this area of work is as rare as phoenix feathers and unicorn horns. In the past year, only the reading movement led by the China Cultural Construction Association has been able to make some effort in promoting reading.

Last year, the Cultural Construction Association initiated the National Reading Movement Conference and the National Reading Competition. The content of the Reading Movement Conference included: one, uniting major publishing institutions across the country to sell their books at half price; two, inviting academic experts to broadcast speeches guiding reading. The effect is unknown, but observing the crowded bookstores during the conference, it may be that there were quite a few people who purchased books and paintings due to the reading movement!

However, this Reading Movement Conference was ultimately more abstract. It may have had considerable power in creating a reading atmosphere, but the effectiveness is ultimately difficult to measure. The Reading Competition was more practical and had a more concrete performance record. Moreover, the extent to which the Reading Competition's results were excellent can also reveal the extent to which Chinese youth generally love to learn.

In the methods of the Reading Competition, there are several points that deserve our special attention. Now I will excerpt them as follows:

1. Registration locations: There are twenty-five locations, including the branches of the Cultural Construction Association in Shanghai, Jiangsu, Beijing, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, Henan, Hebei, Tianjin, Shandong, Shaanxi, Gansu, Qinghai, Fujian, Sichuan, Yunnan, Rehe, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Shanxi, Chahar, and the Northeast.

2. Registration procedures: Fill out two forms, provide three two-inch photos; those who live far away can register by mail; there is no fee; and after joining, you can enjoy a 50% discount when purchasing books from various bookstores.

3. Prizes: Cash or book prizes will be awarded to the top 30 in the university group and the top 30 in the middle school group.

In these methods, it can be said that they are quite perfect, with considerable benefits, and the only obligation is reading. But what were the results of the organization? A glimpse can be seen in the Cultural Construction Association's statistical report:

Registered members: 3,126 in the university group, 2,663 in the middle school group

Members who took the exam: 46 in the university group, 74 in the middle school group

Final score: 88.71 points in the university group, 91.5 points in the middle school group

Lowest score: 38.85 points in the university group, 9.83 points in the middle school group

The fact that the total number of registered members in the country, including both university and middle school groups, is only 5,789 is astonishing enough, but the fact that only 120 members from both university and middle school groups took the exam makes us speechless. Although there are various special reasons for this, we cannot help but acknowledge the scarcity of those who love to learn. And the fact that the best and worst scores are unsatisfactory also goes without saying.

The author believes that although the work of this Reading Competition of the Cultural Construction Association was not successful, it was not wasted at all, and it obtained a great factual lesson, which is how indifferent the general youth of the country are to reading. So not only can we not stop our work because of the poor results of the Reading Competition, but we should also firmly believe that encouraging academic studies and promoting reading are the only urgent tasks for China at present!

Ancient Chinese Economic Thought and System 192

— Huang Zhengzhi

Written by Tageki Jin-i, translated by Wang Xuewen, published by Commercial Press

Studying ancient Chinese economic thought and systems is a very difficult task. Its research methods are nothing more than starting with the following three methods: one is based on ancient historical records, organized and analyzed inductively, and then a general concept is obtained. The second is to focus on the excavation of ancient artifacts, using various methods of geology to study and deliberate, and discover some fragmentary facts of ancient times. Over the years, a correct conclusion can be reached. The third is to refer to ancient historical records, select them, distinguish their authenticity, and then compare the discovered artifacts with each other, and after a thorough investigation and research, make a hypothetical conclusion for future generations to continue to research. These three methods do not contradict each other, but complement each other, and from the perspective of research achievements, they are equally difficult and equally effective.

However, the number of Chinese people engaged in this kind of research is as rare as phoenix feathers and unicorn horns. In a history of world culture, the part about China is still a question mark until now. This is definitely not because Chinese scholars are not progressing, but also because objective reasons have determined it. Political instability, social instability, and the failure to promote the encouragement of academic work all affect the inability to carry out research work. Here, we read Mr. Tageki Jin-i's "Ancient Chinese Economic Thought and System", and we should truly feel ashamed!

Academic work is of course global and knows no national boundaries, but if Chinese people do not study Chinese affairs themselves, but foreign scholars are diligently engaged in it, we are ultimately overwhelmed with remorse and shame.

Mr. Tageki Jin-i's "Chinese Economic Thought and System" uses the first research method that the author mentioned above, which is based on ancient historical records for organization, analysis, and induction. However, in addition to using Chinese ancient books as the main research material, he also compares it with ancient European historical facts for collateral evidence.

In this book, the author's efforts to study one point are, as stated in the "Conclusion": "In ancient and modern times, the ideas of primitive peoples mostly use land and agriculture to symbolize women, and this was also the case in ancient China. For example, women or femininity are used to symbolize land and agriculture; and the orientation and place of worship of such deities adopt the female or feminine approach. …And the characteristics of this kind of thinking are manifested in various ritual systems, and from the official system related to land and agriculture to the system policy, everything is governed by it. It is unnecessary to say that anyone who studies ancient Chinese economic history should not ignore this fundamental idea. …The examination of the development of feudal organization and land system based on this idea accounts for almost half of this article. …" In these few sentences that we excerpt, we can regard them as the main purpose of the author in writing this book: one is the characteristics of ancient Chinese economic thought and institutional organization—namely, feminism—and the other is the economic organization and system based on this characteristic.

For these two points, the author has spent a lot of effort on them, and it is still a hypothetical conclusion—of course, it cannot be said to be a definitive conclusion, which is enough to prove the difficulty of ancient cultural research, and it is very sufficient as an important reference book for those who are interested in studying ancient culture. The book contains 200,000 words, 346 pages, translated by Wang Xuewen, and is priced at two yuan and forty cents, published by Commercial Press.

Clothing, food, housing, and transportation are equally important, and even more so. Therefore, even if the people of our country are not yet qualified to step into the stage of constitutional government, the general intellectuals are already eagerly demanding universal politics. And the Chinese Kuomintang also complied with this demand and promulgated the Draft Constitution of the Republic of China.

In this draft constitution, of course, the political system of the Republic of China is meticulously stipulated on it. When the National Assembly is held on November 12, once it is passed, this political system will be immediately realized. How should we, the general public who demand democracy, research and discuss it now that this political system has been drafted but not yet implemented?

If we want to study the political system, in addition to basing it on Dr. Sun Yat-sen's ideology and the actual experience of the current National Government's five-yuan system, the author believes that it is especially necessary to have a deep understanding and study of the political systems of various countries in the world. Human progress is due to not treading the detours of predecessors; the facts of the past and present are our guiding lights, so the book "Political Systems of Various Countries" jointly compiled by Yang Youjiong and Fu Biao is truly necessary to recommend to you, readers!

In this book of only about 120,000 words, the richness of quality is worth our extraordinary surprise. First, it describes the evolution of various countries; then, it describes the current political institutions of various countries, the origin and rise and fall of the countries; and the functions and composition of their entire political organizations, such as legislative, executive, and judicial institutions; and the nature and rise and fall of political parties; all are briefly explained, so after reading this book, we can have a clear understanding of the national conditions of various countries, the causes and consequences of the changes in political systems, and the current status of political organizations. After having this basic understanding, and then looking back at the current situation in China, and the provisions on the draft constitution, we can not only get a comparative observation, but also get an accurate conclusion that can evaluate its right and wrong, as long as you have some basic knowledge of politics and economics.

At the same time, I feel that this book should not only be introduced to general university and middle school students, but should also be introduced to the general public, because if you want to be a perfect citizen and fulfill your responsibilities as a citizen, you must have basic civic training. This book can be said to be a must-read for every citizen, especially now that the draft constitution has been promulgated but not yet implemented. The book contains 120,000 words, 314 pages, and is priced at 90 cents, published by Zhonghua Book Company.

Treatment Methods for Eczema 199

— (Fuchen)

Eczema can be acute or chronic. If acute eczema is treated incorrectly, it will turn into chronic eczema, which will be prolonged and require a lot of effort. The Service Movement of Peking University Students 203

— Jiawei

The development of events sometimes requires waiting for the arrival of time; however, the progress of time never waits for you for even a minute or a second!

I remember very clearly that during the summer vacation of the previous two sessions, the graduates of various universities in Peking, under the situation of "graduation means unemployment", initiated the organization of the "Professional Alliance". However, as for their subsequent development and results, I have heard little about it and do not know the details.

However, our "Old Man Time" has not been idle and has not been lenient at all: spring has gone, summer has come; then, inevitably, the summer vacation of various schools will also arrive - it is another session!

Although everyone knows that our society is already filled with "excess" (?) job seekers and there is nowhere to accommodate them. "Graduation means unemployment" has become an inevitable trend of the times! However, the students in the shuttle cannot not graduate and leave school, right?

Really, it is another session! The students who are about to graduate must leave the school gate (in fact, the school cannot accommodate them either) and enter the society! Sure enough, it is here again, another "Service Alliance" is still in Peking. According to reports: The Peking University Graduates Service Movement Alliance of this session is scheduled to be established at Chaoyang University on the 26th. It also issued a declaration, which mainly stated: "This service movement is not only for employment, but should continue to demand appropriate solutions to the problem of youth's future, and declare that the motive of the movement is pure..."

We have heard the call to "save the children"; now there are still people shouting to "save the middle school students"! In this way, today, it may be further developed to "save the college students"!

Really, according to the statistics obtained by the Ministry of Education's order to investigate in order to prepare for the relief of unemployed college students, the total number of unemployed graduates from colleges and above in the country in the two years of 1933 and 1934 reached as many as 9,622. This is nearly ten thousand, and it is only the number of people in the previous three years! Adding the current and previous two sessions... it is an alarming number, that is certain!

Here, perhaps our "scholars" will again attribute it to the "incompetence" of the general youth students, but think about it, in today's situation where "graduation means unemployment", who has obtained any guarantee?

Finally, the students of various universities in Peking have consciously organized the "Service Movement Alliance". Sure enough, under the current situation, we cannot expect too much good results from their movement, but we cannot deny the "historical significance" of their movement. Isn't it? Their "pure motives", "not only for employment, but also to continue to demand appropriate solutions to the problem of youth's future"!

Originally, no one would deny that under the current fragmented situation, everything has become a "problem", and at the same time, all problems cannot escape the relationship with society. Moreover, the development of things needs to wait for the opportunity; however, the progress of time will never wait. Young people must seize the historical opportunity and move forward!

About Small Theaters 204

— Yingdai

This is a gratifying piece of news, saying that there are several friends in Shanghai who are working hard on the drama movement and are organizing a weekly experimental small theater, and it has been decided to hold the first public performance at Xinguang on the 31st of this month.

For several years, spoken drama has been in decline for a long time, but this year, spoken drama suddenly seems to be more lively. In the short period of five months, many drama troupes have performed publicly. However, in any case, due to various restrictions on time and space, spoken drama has not yet penetrated the vast masses, which no one dares to deny.

Small theaters have been popular in European and American countries for a long time. The so-called small theater, Little Theatre, is produced out of love for drama. Although the styles are different, the nature is common. The difference between small theaters and general theaters is that the performances are divorced from profit-oriented dramas, and the focus is on trial performances, adopting the repertoire system, Repertoire System. Because ordinary theaters aim at profit, whichever script sells well, they will perform it for a few more days, and if it does not sell well, they will stop performing it. As a result, if there is no box office appeal, even a very good script will be stopped after two or three days. Therefore, how many scripts are performed in a year, and how many days a certain script is performed, is not specified in advance, and everything is determined by objective conditions. As for small theaters, it is not like this. How many scripts are performed in a year has already been arranged in advance, and they are performed accordingly. Even if a certain script has a great box office appeal, the number of days scheduled for the performance will never be extended. On the contrary, even if the box office appeal is very small, it will still be performed according to the catalog.

The small theater originated from Andre Antoine's Free Theatre in France. In the thirty years since then, the entire history of drama can be said to be centered on small theaters. In fact, all the new arts of modern drama, such as light, color, stylization, and synchronization, can only be realized by small theaters. Inspired by Antoine's Free Theatre, Strindbery realized a small stage and a small number of audiences. He established a family theater in Stockholm, the capital of Sweden. In his book "The Art of Drama", he said to us about small theaters like this: "The smaller the theater, the better; the simpler the stage, the better; the more natural the acting, the better; the fewer the characters, the better; the shorter the number of acts, the better; and one-act plays without scene changes are even better. Just one table and two or three chairs, and three or two excellent actors can express the most profound, sharp, and complex soul conflicts that have never been seen on the stage before two or three hundred educated audiences. In the past, in order to make the faces of the performers look better (in fact, uglier), the footlights that were used must be abolished, and only sidelights should be used to illuminate the stage. The act of the actors coming to the front of the stage to greet the audience should be abolished, the stage and the audience seats can be made the same height, and the habit of showing teeth and eating in the dark of the audience seats should be eliminated. The actors' faces do not need to be smeared with makeup, and the stage decoration must have scientific truth." His small theater plan was passed on to Germany, where Max Reinberdt founded the indoor theater, and then passed on to the United Kingdom, the United States, and Russia, all of which made considerable contributions to drama.

Now the stage people in Shanghai are also starting to experiment with small theaters; hearing this news, it seems like getting a new kind of excitement: at the same time, there are endless hopes for this newborn. First, we hope that the small theater will reduce the seat price to a very low level, so that everyone who loves spoken drama can have the opportunity to appreciate the art of drama; at the same time, we also hope that this kind of small theater can exist permanently, performing all year round, and increase from one to countless, so that spoken drama can penetrate into the vast crowd.

The Snake Catcher 205

— Shen Jiaqian

—A Story on the Road—

A sampan boat has just arrived at the dock, with a husband and wife on board. Their boat is so simple, unlike the other sampan boats that are stationed there all year round, some of which live by fishing, some of which make toys, or sell various children's food. Therefore, after the boat arrived, it attracted the attention of their fellow villagers. They, who travel all over the world, often want to inquire about news from their hometown from their fellow villagers, although they know that their hometown is always trapped in floods and famines. Now, a sampan boat that does not even have the tools to make a living has arrived, and they will immediately recall the year they fled, could it be that their hometown has had another major flood? They all surrounded the husband and wife kindly to inquire about the hometown news they wanted to know.

But that couple, like them, had been fleeing from their hometown for many years, and their simple sampan boat had also floated through the small towns of Jiangnan. They did not know anything about the news from their hometown.

The next day, the man also went ashore to do business. He was good at catching snakes and sold a medicine to relieve snake venom. He was carrying a specially made small basket in his hand, with a few dying snakes coiling in the basket, and shouting along the way: "Do you want to catch snakes? Do you want to catch snakes?"

It was a small town in Jiangnan. During the plum rain season, it was not uncommon to find a snake raising its head and wriggling in the corner of someone's wall or under the stove. Sometimes, when walking through a narrow street, a snake would suddenly jump out of the stone crevice under the eaves and scare passersby. When the snake catcher was discovered on the street, someone immediately invited him to catch snakes. He went into people's houses, lay down and crawled along the walls, as if his nose could smell where the snakes were hiding. Wherever there were cracks or small holes, he would apply the antidote he sold on his fingers, reach into the hole to grope, and whistle in his mouth. Within a few minutes, a snake would bite his finger and be caught. He did not accept people's money, only wanted to buy his antidote, but he wanted the snake he caught. He held it by the tail and slammed it hard, hiding it in the bamboo basket. According to him, the antidote was made from snake meat and a medicinal material.

Page 18

In just two days, everyone in the town knew that he was a snake catcher. People who wanted to catch snakes came to the dock early to invite him. The town's richest man invited him to catch snakes everywhere in their high-rise buildings and gardens. He always smelled cautiously with his nose. As long as his hand reached into the hole, he could catch the snake.

He told people: he grew up in the deep mountains since he was a child. He had no father or mother. A huge snake raised him. He lived with snakes every day. Now his nose can especially smell the scent of snakes. In this way, he was regarded as a god, because in those unofficial histories, tigers or human bears often raised an abandoned child, and that child would always be a hero.

The man was busy catching snakes from house to house every day, and he simply couldn't spare himself. A week later, the sampan boat suddenly disappeared. Their fellow villagers did not know where the couple had floated to. But the next day, the town's water patrol team escorted them back to the town. They were thieves on the road. They used the opportunity of catching snakes to peep into people's storage places and steal. Many stolen goods were found on the sampan boat, all of which were stolen in the town within a week.

The snake-catching god was then put in jail.

Stage Play Opposite 206

— Mu Ye

"Damn it, look; look at your pathetic state: how did you manage to get like this? How did you manage to get like this?… I’m asking you! Are you half-dead already? You, you……"

Zhu Da Pangzi (Big Fatty Zhu) was already sweating profusely, his brown face plus the flushed red color, really resembled the roasted meat in the barbecue shop next door! He used his fat hands to wipe the sweat from his head and face, then flicked it onto the ground with a "sha" sound. At the same time, he rudely stretched out his other hand and grabbed the child's ear, pulling it twice as long.

"...Five… jiao… ocean (cents) Ow! Ow!…"

The sallow-faced child was shaking open an old imitation silk robe with holes in it, spiritless, feebly yelling. Unprepared, his ear was suddenly grabbed, and a wave of old spasms arose on his face. His eyes also moistened. He cried out, "Ow! Ow!"

"Humph! I thought you were dead, you son of a bitch! Huh?… You know how to say 'Ow,' huh! You're something else!… Damn it, can't you shout louder? Huh, you're not a young lady… Quick! Put some energy into it! Damn it……"

As Zhu Da Pangzi spoke, he flicked the sweat on his fat hand directly onto the sallow face with a "sha" sound. The child seemed not to notice, not even blinking, only raised one hand to touch his hot, reddened ear. After hesitating for a while, he shook open a pair of faded red trousers.

"Eh… eh yo! One pair… pret… ty… red… pan…ts…"

The voice was still so soft, hoarse and weak, and even carried a crying tone!

"You son of a bitch, shout louder!… Look, you pathetic wimp!… Are you just eating for nothing? Look at them, look! Open your dead eyes, come on, come on! You……"

Indeed, things were not like this on the other side! Not to mention anything else, there were at least fifty or sixty people piled up at the entrance of the shop: there were also ten or so people picking and choosing things there. This really made Zhu Da Pangzi very uncomfortable, as if something were biting at his heart. The people on that side were standing on a tall counter painted shiny and bright. Furthermore, there were two people wearing colorful clothes, much better than the sallow-faced child on this side! They were gesticulating, jumping around, and even stomping on the counter, making it bang: like two fish, their voices were even better, almost as loud as a radio. Listen:

—Hey, hey! This cheongsam, hey! Look, everyone! One ocean! Brand new item, it would cost at least twenty ocean to make a new one! Only buying for one ocean, such a bargain!

—Look carefully, observe carefully! Cheap things are inside!

—Hey, hey! Look at these trousers, on sale cheap! Hey, hey! Sturdy and beautiful! Hey, hey! Selling for only eight jiao (80 cents), eight jiao!

—Observe carefully, look carefully, there are really a lot of cheap things!

—Hey, hey! You… so many, half an ocean!

—Really a lot! Really a lot! If you want to sell, I’ll help you find it!

—Hey, hey!……

"Look, look at them, open your dead cunt eyes, look at them……"

Zhu Da Pangzi shouted, panting with anger. What made him sad was being overshadowed by them, not having any business at all.

"Eh, yo eh! This shirt… three… jiao… zero… eight… fen (cents)…"

Zhu Da Pangzi got even angrier, wiping his sweat twice and flicking it "sha! sha!" onto the sallow face. He quickly went up and grabbed the child's ear again, this time pulling the child all the way to the ground. He pounded with his fists, cursing all the while.

"You son of a bitch, I'm telling you to be half-dead, I'm beating you! Beating you for being like this! Useless, useless! Look at them, look at them……"

People on the street were laughing. Over there, the shouting got even louder and louder! In the voices, it seemed to be mixed with a layer of laughter—as if laughing at Zhu Da Pangzi,

"I, I can't stand it anymore! Can't sleep at night, always shouting like this!… They, they have a lot of people, and they're all adults; I… I can't stand it, I……" After a long time, the sallow-faced child said, sobbing.

"Look, look at your pathetic cunt-like appearance… What are you good for?… Huh?…"

Fists pounded thumpingly on his back!

What to do? Over there, it's so lively, their voices are so good, their shouts are so loud, their feet stomping on the counter making a "dong, dong" sound, so pleasant to hear, like beating a big drum. There are so many people gathered around, but there's no one here, even the hoarse-voiced sallow face is lying on the ground, only able to moan, unable to shout anything.

"Damn it, I just can't accept it, I don't care, business is for everyone! Damn it, I'll do it myself! Let's see who can beat who?……" Zhu Da Pangzi flicked away several handfuls of sweat with a "sha sha" sound, maliciously glanced at the other side, and moved the table forward himself. Then, he placed a stool on the table. Thus, Zhu Da Pangzi, panting with anger, climbed up, making the table creak! creak! He desperately shouted loudly:

"Hey! Hey! We really have cheap things here! Hey! Hey! Come on over! Here… come over!!! You come… look!!! These pan…ts are bran…d new!… Selling for… only two mao (20 cents)… ocean!!!…… They sell things that are all… all bad… things… old goods taken from the… pawn…shops! Hey!… Hey… I… here………"

Zhu Da Pangzi shouted desperately, veins bulging out on his head! Later, he also jumped, he jumped on the small stool! Stomping on the stool making a "deng deng" sound. He was almost turning into a pair of crazy beasts! Sweat flowed down his face, and he kept flicking it away! Finally! He was too excited, tears falling from his eyes, not knowing if it was by accident or what, he fell headfirst from the stool perched on the big table, and fainted! He happened to fall on the sallow-faced child, who only moaned!

Over there, they shouted again:—

—This one! Hey, hey!… Look, look!… Half an ocean! Extremely cheap! Hey, hey! Come on! Too late, you won't get it!

—Look carefully, observe carefully! Cheap things are inside!

Radio Script

Suzhou People (10) 207

— By Gu Wenzong

Sound effects:… Trains speeding along, whistles blowing, people constantly talking in the carriages, waiters from the dining car and vendors calling out to customers to buy food, many passengers, some begging for food, some buying snacks, shouting east and west, a chaotic scene.

Note:… The above section has no fixed dialogue; actors should improvise individually. The most important thing is to avoid making the atmosphere in the carriage too much like a lively temple fair, and to naturally express the real emotions of the train; the actors should be positioned at different distances to create a sense of near and far; actors should avoid interrupting each other, and avoid more than two people speaking at the same time.

Order:… The "vendor" calling out starts from far away and gets closer as the sound effects begin.

Passengers in the distance buy beef, bread, eggs, dried tofu, and chicken cakes.

Passengers nearby shout for the "vendor" to come closer to buy the above items.

The "dining car waiter" nearby asks passengers what they want to eat, and boasts about the delicious and cheap dishes.

Passengers order fried rice, bread, coffee, cocoa, and large dishes, etc.

"Vendor 1 and" the dining car waiter go further away, the sound of passengers talking and the train moving becomes a cacophony.

(Passenger conversations should not be too loud)

Da Jun (takes a cup of tea to drink, tea cup falls, water spills onto Jing Hong’s foot) Ah ya! I’m so sorry! Spilled water on your feet!

Jing Hong It’s alright!

Da Jun Let me wipe it for you.

Jing Hong It’s okay, I’ll do it myself.

Da Jun I’m really too sorry! Got your socks and shoes wet!

Aftersound

Li Changkeng, chief editor of the script "Love Rival," published by Yuanchang Radio Station, No. 7 Sanrang Lane, Caishi Road, Shanghai, is now available, with each issue retailing for five cents. The two scripts, "Northeast Blood" and "Resurrection," also have limited stock remaining, with each type available for five cents by mail.

Comedian Liu Chunshan, recently in response to requests from all walks of life, has specially made public his song lyrics secrets, and has handed them over to Yuanchang Radio Station to publish the "Chunshan Comedy Special," priced at one dime per booklet, with an 80% discount for pre-orders. Those who wish to read Mr. Liu's famous works should make their pre-orders promptly.

Ma Loufen will be restoring the Miaoyin Troupe.

The Yin Yue Troupe has arrived in Shanghai and will be departing for Hankou for the second time in a few days.

After the disintegration of the Chong Sheng Society, a part of the members have contacted theater people from the Lion Roar Drama Society, the Meizhuan Drama Society, etc., to organize the Haiyan Drama Society, which was established yesterday. On June 2nd, they will participate in the Minguang Middle School amusement park performance of "The Newly Arrived Executioner," and on June 6th, the drama "Ward No. 5" for the Wushi Girls' High School farewell graduation ceremony will be directed by Chen Shouqiu, the drama director of the society.

Film

"Waves Washing Sand" Premieres Today 212

Lianhua's First Sound Film

Lianhua Company has been established for several years, and its newly produced films have been welcomed by audiences at home and abroad. However, its previous productions have all been silent films with dubbing. Recently, in order to adapt to the trend, it has focused on creating dialogue sound films. After a year of preparation, it has finally released its first production, "Waves Washing Sand." The film is directed by Wu Yonggang. Based on his past works "The Goddess" and "Little Angel," the excellence of this film's achievements is to be expected. The entire play depicts a criminal who accidentally kills a love rival, leading to being pursued by the police. Leaving his hometown and going far away, he unexpectedly meets the police officer on board. In the middle of the voyage, the ship encounters danger, and the two are adrift on a deserted island. However, due to conflicting interests, they cannot help each other. In the end, they are sacrificed to the power of nature and both perish. The tragedy and passion are extreme. The criminal and the detective are played by Jin Yan and Zhang Zhizhi respectively, both of whom are able to fit their roles appropriately. The film has achieved astonishing success in all aspects and premieres today at the Jincheng Grand Theatre.

Wang Ying Runs a Theater Troupe 213

Some time ago, this publication published an article about Wang Ying going to Japan, and explained that she may have no plays to do there. In fact, Chen Boer's departure will not lead to Wang Ying being assigned to do plays. Because the two of them are likely to clash when they are together. Therefore, even if Wang Ying goes to Japan, it will only be to play around. Now, I don't know if Wang Ying has realized that this trip will not be very pleasant for her. It is said that she has given up this idea. Moreover, recently there was a bizarre piece of news saying that she will be running a theater troupe. If this is true, I think it would be very suitable for her. However, running a theater troupe is not a simple matter, and whether she can pull it off is naturally a question.

Han Langen's Unexpected Harvest 214

Everyone knows that Han Langen is a basic actor of Lianhua. However, Han Langen has roles in Lianhua's "Transformation Girl" and Xinhua's "Peach Blossom Spring Dream." However, it should be a rental, and the rental fee should be stipulated in the contract between the company and the company. But this time, Lianhua rented out Han Langen without asking for money. Therefore, his remuneration only increased. It is estimated that "Transformation Girl" will get 200 yuan, and "Peach Blossom Spring Dream" will get 800 yuan, which is an unexpected harvest for Han Langen.

Reply 217

Messrs. Tong Jianzao and others:

According to recent reports and conversations with friends, this film service agency is probably of a slippery nature. Since you already know that the agency has had similar fraudulent incidents in the Gongqing Building before, there is no need to try it out. Film companies officially recruit actors and never collect security deposits. This is my reply.
